$ TODO proposal -- Alb aorists in -s- (and others?) augmented with material drawn from past indicative forms of PIE (x)es-: s-esm̩ B(> səsa > shë), es (> heh), [-∅, or -id?], -s-omos  [-(ː)më] (note 1PL kjeshmë "was", -sete, -sonti . This explains Gheg outcomes in 1sg -ā, 2sg -ae ... etc. 

$ MAJOR MORPHEMES IN USE -- see morphemics file for more

$ VERBAL INFLECTION, not including many grade changes 
	$ preference for these forms: 
		$ participle 
		$ 1sg = 3sg >>> 3pl >> 2sg = 1pl ; generally exclude 2pl as ffit is usually replaced esp in present
		$ 2sg imperative occasionally when most secure
		$ present > aorist >>> past imperfect >> rest 
		$ indic > subj , but in subj 3sg >> 1sg = 3pl >>>>>>> rest 
		$ mediopassive only when diachronically informative
	$ partciple form -- 	
			$ generally aorist stem + -u/onm̩, -m̩, -nm̩ 
			$ Source of -onm̩ ː -onm̩ is perhaps from -ontm̩, accusative of participle formant -onts, with the -tm̩ reanalyzed as beng tacked on 
				$ for source of backformation here - {note addition onto 3sg and 3pl inflectional forms of 3sg -ta < -tod 3nsg.nom/acc or -tm̩, and 3pl -ta{s} < teχ{-s}, npl }
				$ alternatively, this is -o-nóm, thematic o + PIE deverbal adjectival suffix -nóm -- cf Sanskrit -ana, Proto-Gmc -anã  
					$and cases where it's -nm̩ are just -nóm 
	$ person-number notes: 
		$ 2pl generally lost in present
		$ 3pl -nt{i} endings often extended to -nta <  -nteχs , -ntm̩? 
		$ 3sg: often become null or just i-mutation; unlike 2sg but like 3sg, feature secondarily grammaticalized elements
			$PAlb -ta {-tm̩, teχ?} in singular often in subjunctive {ketë "have.3sg.subj"}, occasoinally indicative presnet {thotë "say.3sg" etc.},
			$past.impf -te < -toi? -tōd?  {cf. imperativ3 3sg. -tōd}
			$aor: 3smg distal pronoun may be grammaticalized in as -i; -u after i- final stems
				$ the OAlb forms like suall for sjell for soll-a/i, duallë/duall for doll-a/i need an explanation... currently going with -id, consider -swe or -swos or -sos.
	̩$ present: often extended with nasal progressive -ne after thematic vowel, often reduced to nj later. 
		$ may be extended in -i-, likely originally derivational
			$ sporadic stem extension in -ot-i- 
		$ 2pl nearly always a secondary formation not datable back to APA let alone PIE ; from -nū imperative
		̩$ i-mutation in 2sg and 3sg became morphologized by Late Proto-Albanian; ditto for imperative, imperfect, occasional 3sg aorist in -t- 
	$ aorist: 
		$ prefix augment xe- , apply when reasonable
		$ root: lengthened grade in many cases {see Orel 2000}; 
		$ stem suffixes:
			$ sigmatic -es 
			$ -v- endings ; -es + -w- as seen in Latin -ui it seems
				$ cf. Toch -sw-?
			$-t- aorists: decide
			$ -r/n- aorist: just rebracketed final -n from stem
		$ endings: typically secondary, but forms of "BE" are often grammaticalized in before they apply
	$ imperfect: often -es-ne- + BE , but -tōd added to 3sg
	$ mediopassive: from iterative -sceti, but EXTENDED 
		$ for 1SG and 2SG : -sc- + PRIMARY ending + SECONDARY ending + "A" element  {see below} 
			$ "A" : mysterious item reflected as schwa, from o or m̩ or maybe oi {cf Gk nact -omai?}
				$ or maybe the χe from the acutal Indo-European middle?
		$ e.g. 1sg -sc- + primary -oχ + secondary -m + A
			$ -x-ō-m-a > xœ̄ma > Old Albanian -hemë, -emë > -hem, -em, h lost after some consonantal stems
		$ 2sg: -sc- + e-si + s + A > -xɛ́sɩsa > -xɛ́ssa > OAlb {h}eshë > {h}esh
			 $single s would disappear if this gemination didn't occur. 
			 	$maybe 3SG is geminated too but we can't tell either way.
		$ 3SG : -sc- + SECONDARY ENDING + the same "A" element
		$ 3sg: -sc- + et + A  > .. > OAlb -hetë 
		$ 3PL : actually just reflects -sconti with i-mutation? 

		$ 1pl and 2pl : from optative -scoyme and scoyte, with some i-mutating element added at end to make the final -e become -i for both, maybe an -i or-si

		$ PERHAPS all hte endings actuallz come from sc+optatives...
	$iterative -sceti with normal forms grammaticalized in words like 1sg njoh/3sg njeh; shoh/sheh/ etc.

$NOMINAL INFLECTION
	$ per Orel 2000 and it seems others agree, resonant final noun-stems become -o- stems.
	$ plural i-mutation grammaticalized by Late Proto-Albanian
	$ unlike Latin, it seems nominative is often reflected: masc ∅ < -o-s, neut -ë < -a < -m̩, -óm rarely; fem -ë < a < ā < eχ
	$ pluralizing, perhaps og collective, -ëra/-na < -ina per Orel 2000(:229), which causes i-mutation, from a "collectivizing" PIE -īna he says. I'm treating this as from adjectivalizing -iHn(-os) + collectivizing -eχ. Since feminine of the latter is listed without accent, ot putting it on, for now. 
	$ MPL i-mutating -ër/-ën treated as from -énes, plural of PIE suffix *-éːn forming nouns of roots, more in line with De Vaan 2004: 71; Schumacher 2013(:2019) has it via -inih; Orel 2000(: 230) instead has a proposed PIE *-ino for these. 
	$ -nj- mpl form   

$ NOMINAL DERIVATION
	$ -i-eh2 as source of collective/feminine derivational suffix -í, def. -ía
	$ $ using -akʷyos rather than -ikʷyos -- makes more sense for -u(a/o/e)s in enlargument from o-stem verbs. Also Durrës. 
	$ material afix -ixnos 
	$ locative -i 
	$ deverbal -{e/o}dhieχ
	$ -tieχ
	$ -trom 
	$ deverbal -mn̩ > ma
	$ abstract verbal substantive -- im-o/eχ
	$ -ulós 
	$ -icos > th, can i-mutate
	$ -iqos > k, can i-mutate 
	$ -us-s > -ush, became diminutive; occasional -os-s >  ësh 
	$ -eχ feminizing, may be redundant: mother root + this 
	$ -ibʰ-o/m̩/eχ -- or eb-~~? 
	$ -steχ from "stand", instrumental i-st- ... -- Orel 2000: 160-1.

	$k1-h3-i- "sharp, sharpen, whet" 
c xʷ i q ˈe χ , θ ˈi k ə , θ ˈi k ə $knife. Bardhyl and Imberciadori 2024: https://www.dpwa.gwi.uni-muenchen.de/dictionary/?lemmaid=28257. Orel 1998: 477-8 as from a PIE *k¹éi-, cf to Sanskrit śiśati "to whet", Armenian sur "sharp; knife". Possibly loaned from CPA *t͡siːkɑ > Lat. sīca. On the basis of the Sanskrit śā, PIE k1eh3-i- 'sharpen' -- NIL 411 -- hence Latin cō-t-em, English ho-ne, Ancient Greek kô-nos. Unique extension in -kos. 
	$k1-h3-k2

c xʷ ˈe q e n e s , θ ˈæ k ə̃ ɾ̃ ə , θ ˈɛ k ə ɾ $rye. From a plural of thak. Demiraj 1997: 393.

	$k1-h3-{e}{s}tr-

Orel 1998: 471 as from PAlb *tsestra cognate to Skt śastrá 'knife, sword', but PROPOSAL LARYNGEAL METATHESIS creates same outcome as o-grade gives the same Skt outcome -- PROPOSAL going with this. Demiraj 1997: 391 has ϑat(Vr)- < QIE *ḱh3-to/t(e)r-, with the -d- explained as 'dialectal'; NIL 411, 413 follows him and connects it to Latin, supposedly from Gaulish, catanus 'cedar juniper', and Latin Catō, Catonis.  
kʷ m̩ c xʷ ˈe t r o  m , k ə θ ˈa t ɾ̩ , k θ ˈa t ə ɾ $talons {bird of prey}. May be from same item as above. Unclear Demiraj 1997: 391. From kʷu- perhaps same as above, though Demiraj has a different reconstruction for it. Increasingly the i-mutated plural këthetër. PROPOSAL that this reflects the instrumental deverbal noun derivational affix -trom

		$k1-h3-r-h1- sourdough
c xʷ ˈe r x bʰ o s , θ ˈa ɾ b , θ ˈa ɾ b $yeast. Uncited but clear -bh- > -b derivative in line with others listed by Orel 2000:152, including *tharbë.  Medial laryngeal may not be necessary but included for consistence with thark. 
c xʷ ˈe r x bʰ m̩ t m̩ , θ ˈa ɾ b ə t ə , θ ˈa ɾ b ə t $sour. Og tharbë < bh- per Orel 2000: 152, thensuffixed in nyja -t-, using -m̩ per adjectival ending policy. Romanian sarbăd, with voicing of the -t- to -d- also seen in Beskidy mtn range from beskai tai, per Orel 1998: 472. Medial laryngeal may not be necessary but included for consistence with thark. 
c xʷ ˈe r x bʰ t m̩ , θ ˈa ɾ t ə , θ ˈa ɾ t ə $sour, related to the above. Orel 1998: 472.
c xʷ ˈe r x m o s , θ ˈa ɾ m , θ ˈa ɾ m $sourdough, yogurt ferment. Cf Lith šarmas "lye". Cabej  1986 VII: 202. 1998: 472. Medial laryngeal may not be necessary but included for consistence with thark.

	$ɟ-n-w knee 
ɟ n ˈu n o s , ɡ ʎ ˈũː , ɟ ˈu $knee. Proto-Alb *glũː -- Lab/Cham/Arb/Arv glū, Gheg gjû. May be loan from Celtic, but short vowel is inherited in Alb and long in Celtic making that less likely. Hyllested & Joseph 2022; Lopuhaa 2015; Demiraj 1997: 190. Arbanasi gynj, ARb glu, glunjë, occasional Gheg gũ. OIr. glún ‘knee’; Go. kniu ‘knee’. 

	$g1-l-h1 
ɟ l̩ x i r ˈo s , ɡ ʎ ˈɛ ɾ , ɟ ˈɛ ɾ  $dormouse. Related to the dormouse/sister-in-law word. NATIVE PROPOSAL, via caland -ro usurping s. Cf. AGK galéē. Rejected etymology from Latin glis, glirem: dormouse. May be native instead.  Attributed to "another stage of contacts" in which Lat ī > Alb e per Orel 2000: 34. Bonnet 1998: 380. Arbëreshë has lir and ler; these may be later Romance loans (cf. Neapolitan gliero, gliro; Fr. loir, etc.) or a separate etym/item (see below). Some Gheg has ger, and some dialects have ger instead as meaning "squirrel" (Bonnet 1998: 247).

$gh1-

$gh1-dh   "earth"
ɟʰ dʰ ˈoː m , ð ˈɛː , ð ˈɛ $earth,ground, accusative sg inheritance. Not nasalized in Gheg. Messapic da (da-matura). Greek chthw̄n, Toch tkam. Demiraj 1997: 155; NIL 91. But see below.
dʰ ˈe ɟʰ x ˈoː s , ð ˈɛː , ð ˈɛ $earth, ground-- nominative sg inheritance. Hamp 1990: 291. Neri/Demiraj 2021 https://www.dpwa.gwi.uni-muenchen.de/dictionary/?lemmaid=18233#kapitel6 as PIE dʰéɟʰom-/dʰɟʰm- > dʰɟʰóm 'earth' but feminine, however present nom/acc sg dhē from a dʒōs wiht -s auslaut. Schumacher '13: 224 convincingly argues for this as the nominative of the accusative dʰéɟʰōm that goes to dhe too, parallel in Toch ksās nom vs ksām acc. Therefore, using both of these in APIELex, tentatively, favoring the dʰɟʰ form that Demiraj seems to have mobved to as well. See above. Cf also Ringe 2006. Witczak '16: 41 attributes this as the source Agk dē. 
ɟʰ dʰ ˈoː m i χ , >* , ð ˈɛ m j ɛ $caterpillar. Tentative (TODO check). Cf Orel 1998: 81 (apud Neri 2021 @ https://www.dpwa.gwi.uni-muenchen.de/dictionary/?lemmaid=18233)

ˌn̩ bʰ u l ˈo s , ˈa v u lˠ , ˈa v u lˠ $vapor. My proposal, but based on considering the established attribution to *nebʰ-el-o/a in NIL 500; Hamp 1975ː 449 apud NIL 503; note also orel 1998(ː12) for whom it reflects a n̩(∅)bʰ-(u)lo "l stem", and Huld 2005(ː59) for whom it is a compound of n̩bʰo- and a *wl̩Ho. However, this derivation in n̩∅bʰ-ulos would appear to have regular correspondence to Messapic at-abulus, Latin nebul-a, and Germanic *nebulaz (Old English nifol, Old High German nibul, nebul), and be an unsurprising formal and derivational extension of the well attested stem n(e)bh-o- (Greek néphos, OCS nébo, Sanskrit nábhas). Romanian abure is more consistent with this.

χ ˈe r m n m̩ , ɦ ˈa ɾ n ə , ˈa ɾ n ə $patch. PROPOSAL of cognacy to Epic Greek ɦár-menos {Rix 2001 LIV: 269-270}, perhaps AGK ɦarm-onia {De Vaan 2008: 54}. $kw- pronoun outcomes
kʷ ˌo j , >* , c ə $that. Demiraj 1997: 80, but he notes it's "at least equally likely" that it reflects a loan from Latin que.
kʷ e , >* , s $not. Cf. French ne... que construction. Demiraj 1997: 276. From relative/interrogative pronoun kʷe (form could have been kʷís, kʷíd; assuming nominative...). NIL 280. 
kʷ ˈi x , >* , s ˈi $how. From instrumental. Demiraj 1997: 353. Schumacher '13ː 225. Latin quī, English why, etc. 
kʷ ˈi x χ ˈe n , >* , s ˈa $how much. Demiraj 1997: 353. Or from kwix-χew. 
kʷ ˈe m x t i s , >* , s ˈɛ n d $object, thing. THIS IS A PROPOSAL: kʷe "that, which", + mxtis "measure" (favorable as it is known to be extant in Albanian mot "time, weather", moshë "age", mat/mas "measure"). Attributed to a cjom tom by Orel 1998: 394 (but this is phonologically suspect); Majer 2024(:220) to a PIE **kʷendʰ (other reflexes -- locate?) but this seems preferable. 
kʷ i d , >* , t͡ʃ $what, which. Orel 1998: 52. May actually specifically reflect preconsonantal outcome (cf. kʷe/-id/-is > s' "not" for consideration). May be short for çfarë below (wiht sporeχ > farë) . Various Gheg forms: sha, qa, çi, çin ,çe, çer, ça, çar... (TODO CONSIDER? -- cka? wiht -r as in kurrë, po-r?)
kʷ i d s p o r ˈe χ , >* , t͡ʃ f ˈa ɾ ə $what, which. See above. 
kʷ ˈi s , >* , s ˈɛ $that, as. Demiraj 1997: 353. AGk tis, Latin quis/quid, MWelsh pe, Old Irish cid, Skt kis, Avestan ciš.


kʷ ˌo , >* , k ə $proximal particle, in proximal pronouns; 'here'-. Huld 1984: 84-5. From kwu- per Demiraj 1997: 217, who also floats Latin eccum. Gheg kã/kõ 'here' handled below. Neri 2023 has it from eccum as well --https://www.dpwa.gwi.uni-muenchen.de/dictionary/?lemmaid=21884. 
kʷ ˈo x , >* , k ˈɛ $where, relative conjunction. Schumacher '13:223, 243 . 
kʷ ˌo t ˈo m , k ə t ˈãː , ... $neutsg nom/acc proximal pronoun, extant in Malësorisht, cf. Lindon file on pronouns (likewise distal atâ).

kʷ ˈo s m i , k ˈãː , k ˈə $'here'; PROPOSAL (TODO unless found) as being from locative form of PIE *kwo-. 
kʷ ˌo j , >* , c ˌə $relative pronoun. Demiraj 1997: 80, who notes it's just as likely from Latin que (or, Latin quī -- that was Orel, probably, or Bonnet?)
kʷ ˈo m , k ˈãː , k ˈə $whom (acc). Gheg kâ, incl Bogdani. Schumacher 2013: 212. LPA kˈãː. 
kʷ ˈo m t o , k ˈãː n t , k ˈə n d $whom (acc, long). Gheg kân(d).  Demiraj 1997: 218, he nevertheless has this reservation: "The derivation of kënd < kwom-tom is problematic since *-nt- yields -n- in the acc.sg.m. of noun paradigms. Also, the oldest Geg texts have acc.sg. ke, ka (nasalized vowels), and also kun, kana (Buz.). Hence, -d in kënd must be a later addition. Its earliest occurrence seems to be in the indefinites (e.g. Bogd. as ... kand), hence one might think of a reduced form of -do ‘will’, as in the later form kushdo."

kʷ o s ˈu χ s , k ˈyː , k ˈy $prox.msg. Schumacher '13: 213. 
kʷ ˈo s s o s , >* , k ˈu ʃ $who (nom.). From 'who (is) that'. Schumacher '13: 213, 264.  Hackstein 2021 at DPEWA https://www.dpwa.gwi.uni-muenchen.de/dictionary/?lemmaid=9537. Demiraj 1997(: 228) attr'd it to a *kʷu-sm̥. Messapic kos. 
kʷ ˈu , >* , k ˈu $where. Demiraj 1997: 226.
kʷ ˈu n t o , k ˈũ n t , k ˈu n d $somewhere. Demiraj 1997: 226 via < *kwuN-to-.. But see his remarks wrt kënd "whom". 
kʷ ˈu r , k ˈuː ɾ , k ˈu ɾ $when. Demiraj 1997: 227; Demiraj & Neri 2024 ; Schumacher '13: 217.
kʷ ˈr̩ , k ˈuː ɾ , k ˈu ɾ $when. PROPOSAL: zero grade form of kʷó +-r, rather than this kʷúr which appears only extant elsehwere in Armenian and Baltic (where r̩ > ur might also be internally motivated.) 
kʷ ˈu r n e , >* , k ˈu r ə $never, as from kʷur 'where' + ne/o 'not'. Demiraj 1997: 227; Demiraj & Neri 2024. However see PROPOSAL BELOW in align with zero grade derivation of kur above.

w ˈeː r t i bʰ e χ , v ˈɔ ɾ b ə , v ˈɔ ɾ b ə $type of clay pot. Attributed to an "early" Slavic loan in wˈɑrɪbɑ by Orel 1998: 514, but this stem does not appear in Derksen 2008, which only has var-i- "to heat (vb.)" and varʊ "heat". Demiraj 1997: 424 attributes this and vorbull "whirlpool" to a PIE wērb{ʰ}- but this root is unknown. Suffixation in -bh- is possible; applied the general pattern seen in Orel 2000: 151-2 for ibha obha suffixation as also seen in Balto-Slavic. The root, if Demiraj is right on the semantic development, is much more likely {PROPOSAL!} PIE *wert- {e.g. Lat verto} "to turn", with the -t- lost to cluster simplification. 
w ˌeː r t i bʰ u l ˈo s , v ˈɔ ɾ b u lˠ , v ˈɔ ɾ b u lˠ $whirlpool, vortex. Demiraj 1997: 424. Replaced unknown werbh- root with wertibh-, for reasons on this see vorbë.

$ped-s "foot"
p ˈe d s i , p ˈɔ ʃ , p ˈɔ ʃ $below -- bound root in përposh "downwards, underneath" and rëposh "below". NIL 527: cognate to Old Irish ís "below", Old Welsh is "below", Umbrian abl.sg persi "from the foot". Lengthening via Winter's law per NIL 532. Hamp 1991: 74 instead proposes an adverb pēd-si under a pēd-tjo which is rejected for its claims of underlying the Baltic by the NIL 532. Demiraj 1997 and Orel 1998 both discuss influence from Latin pos poste "behind", if not borrowing, which leaves some semantic questions. Schumacher '13ː 221 prefer -su. 
p ˈe d s u t e r o s , p ˈɔ ʃ t ɾ̩ , p ˈɔ ʃ t ə ɾ $beneath, underneath, lower, lowest {adverb}. Otherwise from Latin posterus -- see ALLAPS -- per Demiraj apud NIL 532. TODO PROPOSED derivation in -teros oppositoinal adj suffix {e.g. Skt ud 'above' ~ uttara 'upper'}.  
p e d s u t ˈe r o s , p ə ʃ t ˈi e̯ ɾ ə , p ə ʃ t j ˈɛ ɾ ə $deep, deep down {adj}. Otherwise some relationship to Latin posterior etc. NIL 532. 
p ˈe d s u t m̩ , p ˈɔ ʃ t ə , p ˈɔ ʃ t ə $downwards. Lengthening per Winter's law per Hamp apud NIL 532 -- TODO lexicalize? From locative ped-si "at the foot", with adjectival derivational -tm̩, thus cognate to Vedic patsutas -- Lipp 243 apud NIL 532.  Demiraj 1997 has it from Latin, with some semantic difficulties.

	$prior o-grade 
dʰ ˌo r ɟʰ ˈe j o χ , d ˈæ ɾ ð , d ˈɛ ɾ ð $spill.1sg.pres.act.indic. From root o-grade causative of *dʰrɟʰ turn -- to make turn. Aorist of same item reflects in Armenian darjaw 'invert, return'. May also relate to Arm. durgn "wheel". Rix LIV 2001: 146. Neri and Demiraj 2021 https://www.dpwa.gwi.uni-muenchen.de/dictionary/?lemmaid=17697 -- they note it's a "Armeno-Albanian" exclusive isogloss but don't note the Armenian there. These two alone are listed for dʰerĝʰ "to turn" in Rix LIV 2001: 146 though.  Orel 1998{:60} notes un-i-mutated dardh in Buzuku and Budi. Orel connects this to Lith darděti "rattle", Latv dārdêt "creak", W. go-dyrddu "mumble", which he thinks {Unnecessarily} is "onomatopoeic".

$ dʰreχɟ "berry, fruit-bearing tree" -- PROPOSAL -- PAlb dra̋ð{-əza} "strawberry", darða "pear, pear tree";

		$ Lat frāgum "berry"; nasal extension in Lat fraxinus "ash", PCelt drageno "sloe" {Gaul drageno > Fr. dial. dren; OIr draigen; MW draen }, perhaps Slav dernɪ "cornel" ; perhaps via sigmatic extension Skt dhrā́kṣā

dʰ r ˈe χ ɟ s e χ , d ɾ ˈæ ð ə , d ɾ ˈɛ ð ə $strawberry. Topalli 2017: 82. Tosk dredhë, dialectal Tosk dreth/drethë, Arbëreshë drethe; South Gheg drethe , East Gheg drathe {NOT I-MUTATED}, drenth. For Topalli 2017: 82 apparently from a *dʰreh₂ǵ-seh, thus cognate to Sanskrit dhrākṣā "grape, vine" {also with drāks̩ā} and via the root, Latin frāgum "strawberry". This causes vowel quality problems though-- alternative below. 
dʰ r ˈe χ ɟ s ˈe dʰ i e χ , d ɾ ˈæ ð ə z ə , d ɾ ˈɛ ð ə z $strawberry; cord, string. Derived form more common today. Appears also as Gheg drellëz. Setting aside the 'cord, string' senses as etymologically different, handling as diminutive in -{i?e?}dhieχ with stress retraction then i-mutation.  Otherwise may have to relate it to the -s- thematic form in Skt drā́k-ṣ-ā, or an -icos/eχ ending? 
dʰ ˈr̩ χ ɟ ˈe dʰ i e χ , d ɾ ˈæ ð ə z ə , d ɾ ˈɛ ð ə z $strawberry, cord, string. PROPOSAL revising view of Topalli '17 in *dʰreh₂ǵ-seh, that this is has no sigmatic suffix and is ZERO-grade, to explain the vowel quality, with addition of edʰia. Cognacy to Latin frāgum "berry" and frāxinus "ash" {frāg-s-inos}, plus Celtic dragenos whence OIr draigen, Gaulish dragenos > Fr. dren -- for this as a reflex of zero grade with laryngeal in Celtic and Italic respectively see Stifter 2018: 1195 and Meiser  2018:746 in IE handbook. This is PROPOSAL for Latin fraxinus as actually a cognate to this rather than bhrHɟ-s--enos? 

$DARDHË "pear" issue -- attributed to substratal darda by Demiraj 1997: 121, see APBalkLex, alternatives below

With diff placement of nasal infix to before the exʷ, forming str̥néh₃ti, cognate to Lat stern-o-, AGk stórnūmi, Celt starnat i > Welsh saru, OIr sernaid , Skt str̩n̩āti , Avestan stərə̯nājti etc. Hoewver this doesn't work for Alb as it would give a long ō > œ. Demriaj notes a *str(h3)-eh1- as the stem. 
s t e r xʷ ˈe x w e q e χ , >* , ʃ t ɾ ˈɔ f k ə $den. FORM PROPOSAL. Following Demiraj 1997: 379 on relation to shtroj. Orel 1998: 442 attributed to shtrohë/shtrofë instead. PROPOSAL for exact derivation per Demiraj 97: Drawn from shtroj from a short participle (Orel 2000: 215-6) off of a -w- aorist (Orel 2000: 199-200), appended with the back velar suffix (Orel 2000: 156-8).

s r̩ χ ɢ ˈu s s o s , r ˈu ʃ , r ˈu ʃ $grape; Dubrovnik. From oblique form of ancestor of Greek rhˈōx. Seems to be -uss- suffix cf Orel 2000:158-9. Orel 1998: 391. Alternatively loaned from Greek rhox -- Schumacher 2013: 213. As old name of Dubrovnik, Latin Ragusium, Byz Greek (10th c. Const. Porphyrogen.) Rhaoússin, Rhaoúsa. Italian Ragusa seems to be from Dalmatian Ragusa, not recorded until the 13th c. Buzuku has Rush, could last that as gold form for Old Albanian as it was likely inherited to that point. Cabej 1986 II: 102-3,  Orel 1998: 391: reflects the early Albanian loss of the intervocalic voiced stop before the contraction of vowels. On Ragusa, Bonnet 1998: 166. Also Huld 1986:249 as following Alb-Makedonian accent rules.

s ˈe r p o n o s , ɟ ˈa ɾ p ə̃ ɾ̃ ə , ɟ ˈa ɾ p ə ɾ $snake, NSG. N-stem it seems. Gheg gjarpën. Demiraj 1997: 183; Matzinger 2013: 209. Gheg gjarpën. A sonorant stem that became o-grade per Orel 2000: 218, a point Schumacher (2013: 209) also implies although while Orel has -a as the reflex of Proto-Albanian -os, Schumacher has -ʉh; Demiraj also seems to agree. Seems to show root accent etymologically, given gj- rather than sh- outcome. Consider shtërpinj below. Orel 200(:49, 61, 218) has -ena < -enos, Schumacher (2013: 209) has a PAlb SG -anʉh and pl -ánai (; > Buzuku gjarpënë and PL gjarpanjë) which is presumably < -onos, -onoi, while Demiraj is unsure: "-e/ono". Buzuku's variety seems to reflect -o- > -a- but Tosk purals appear to be gjarpinj, gjarpij, (and gjarpra, likely from n-stem acc pl amphikinetic -V́nn̩s)... which appear if anything to suggest -e- for plural. Unclear. Cognatesː Latin serpens, Ancient Greek ἑρπετόν (herpetón) and Sanskrit सर्प sarpá

l o n t 'e χ , l ˈɑ̃ n t ə , l ˈə n d ə $mass, acorn, gland, lens. Imberciadori 2024 @DPEWA: lëndë. Rejected Latin etymologies in glandem and lentem: Equated to French gland which means both by Bonnet 1998 -- "acorn" is the only meaning supported in Newmark 1998(:452)). Bonnet 1998(: 249) -- lëndë is Tosk; Cham and some Tosk have lënde; Gheg has lênn, lend, and land (land as northern Gheg ?). Meyer 1891(:243) notes the plural lëndre in Cham/Arv in Greece, and Romanian ghindă, and Aromanian and Megl. glîndã. Çabej 1960 prefers a native etymology, connected to lënde "lens, lentil", which Bonnet 1998(:250) sees as more likely from Latin lentem itself. However, this latter lënde "lens, lentil" is not in Newmark 1998(; 452), which lists lënde as "matter, timber, acorn". It appears that form in -a was reflected in Balkan Romance, and much of the rest of Romance --REW p281-2 (n.3778). Possibly native instead, cf. PIE lenteχ, cf Mallory and Adams 2006: 161 -- However Mallory and Adams root would end up as lënë -- better option necessary TODO.. Final -ë may be analogical from plural, or bc movement into the -a- feminine class. Could also be from Romanian gʎɨndə forms themselves. Rejected lentem etymology :Analogical -ë in modern form? Or from a *lentā- perhaps even native? Lat. lens, lentis is a rival etymology for Cabej's view that it's from Lat. glans, coming from Bonnet 1998(: 249-50).
